This Supplement dated August 12, 2024 (the “Su pplement”) supplements the above referenced 
Official Statement dated August 1, 2024 (the “Official Statement”) in respect of the above-captioned bonds 
(the “Series 2024 Bonds”).  This Supplement constitutes an integral part of the Official Statement and 
should be read in conjunction with the Official Statement.  Capitalized terms used but not otherwise defined 
herein shall have the meanings assigned to such terms in the Preliminary Official Statement. 
The name of the Trustee in respect of the Series 2024 Bonds is Zions Bancorporation, National 
Association.  Each reference to “Zions Bank, a Di vision of ZB, National Association” is replaced with 
“Zions Bancorporation, National Association.” 
In all other respects, the Official Statement is  unchanged.  This Supplement, the Appendices and 
the forepart of the Official Statement together constitute the entire Official Statement.

The $29,675,000 City of Cleveland, Ohio, Water Pollution Control Revenue Bonds, Series 2024 (the “Series 2024 Bonds”) 
are 
special obligations of the City of Cleveland, Ohio (the “City”) issued under and secured by the provisions of the Master 
Trust Agreement, dated April 14, 2016 (the “Master Trust Agreement”), by and between the City and Zions Bank, a Division of 
ZB, National Association, Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania, as trustee (the “Trustee”), as supplemented by the Second Supplemental 
Trust Agreement, dated August 15, 2024, by and between the City and the Trustee (the “Second Supplemental Trust Agreement” 
and together with the Master Trust Agreement, as amended and supplemented from time to time, the “Trust Agreement”), to 
provide funds to the City’s Department of Public Utilities, Division of Water Pollution Control to (i) pay Capital Costs relating 
to the acquisition, construction and improvement of the System, (ii) fund the Debt Service Reserve Requirement for the Series 
2024 Bonds and (iii) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds. See “
Appendix  B - d efinitions  And  s ummAry  of  CertAin  
t erms  And  p rovisions  of  the  t rust  Agreement .” 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be secured under the Trust Agreement, on a parity with all Outstanding Bonds, and any 
Additional Bonds issued thereunder, by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the Special Funds (all as defined herein).  
See “
s eCurity  And  s ourCes  of  p Ayment  of  the  Bonds .”
Interest on the Series 2024 Bonds is payable semiannually on each May 15 and November 15, beginning May 15, 2025.  The 
Series 2024 Bonds will be initially issued as fully registered bonds under a book-entry system, and will be registered initially in 
the name of Cede & Co., as nominee for The Depository Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”).  Purchases of book-
entry interests in the Series 2024 Bonds will be made in denominations of $5,000 and any integral multiple thereof.  DTC, or its 
nominee, will receive all payments with respect to the Series 2024 Bonds from the Trustee.  DTC is required by its rules and 
procedures to remit such payments to participants in DTC for subsequent disbursement to the owners of book-entry interests.  
Holders of book-entry interests in the Series 2024 Bonds will not receive physical delivery of bond certificates.  The Series 
2024 Bonds in certificated form as such will not be transferable or exchangeable, except for transfer to a nominee of DTC or 
as otherwise described in this Official Statement.  Principal of and redemption premium, if any, and interest on, the Series 2024 
Bonds will be paid to Cede & Co. as the registered owner.  See “
Appendix  g – B ook -e ntry  o nly  s ystem ” hereto.
The Series 2024 Bonds are subject to optional and mandatory sinking fund redemption prior to maturity as described 
herein. See “t he  s eries  2024 Bonds  – Redemption of the Series 2024 Bonds.”
The Series 2024 Bonds will be special obligations of the City and will not represent or constitute a general 
obligation, bonded indebtedness or a pledge of the general credit or taxing power of the City, the State of Ohio 
or any political subdivision thereof.  The holders of the Series 2024 Bonds will not have the right to have excises 
or taxes levied by the City, the State of Ohio or the taxing authority of any political subdivision thereof for the 
payment of debt service charges. See “
CertAin  i nvestment  ConsiderAtions  And  r isk  fACtors  – Limited Obligations.”
The Series 2024 Bonds are offered when, as and if issued by the City, and accepted by the Underwriters, subject to the 
opinion on certain legal matters relating to their issuance of Squire Patton Boggs (US) LLP, Bond Counsel.  Certain legal 
matters will be passed upon for the City by Mark D. Griffin, its Chief Legal Officer and Director of Law, and Dinsmore 
& Shohl LLP, as disclosure counsel to the City.  Certain legal matters will be passed upon for the Underwriters by Calfee, 
Halter & Griswold LLP.  The Series 2024 Bonds are expected to be available for delivery to DTC on or about August 15, 2024.

REGARDING THIS OFFICIAL STATEMENT 
General 
This Official Statement does not constitute an offering of any security other than the original 
offering of by the City of Cleveland, Ohio (the “City”) of its $29,675,000 Water Pollution Control Revenue 
Bonds, Series 2024 (the “Series 2024 Bonds”).  No person, other than the Director of Finance of the City, 
has been authorized by the City or Stifel, Nicolaus & Company, Incorporated on behalf of itself and as 
representative for the Underwriters identified on the front cover (collectively, the “Underwriters”), to give 
any information or to make any representation other than as contained in this Official Statement.  Any other 
representation not so authorized should not be relied upon as having been given or authorized by the City 
or the Underwriters.  This Official Statement does not constitute an offer to sell or the solicitation of an 
offer to buy, and there shall not be any sale of the Series 2024 Bonds by any person in any jurisdiction in 
which it is unlawful to make such offer, solicitation or sale. 
This Official Statement includes the front cover page and all appendices hereto.  The information 
in this Official Statement is provided by the City in connection with the original offering of the Series 2024 
Bonds.  Reliance should not be placed on any other information publicly provided, in any format including 
electronic, by the City for other purposes, including general information provided to the public or to portions 
of the public.  The information and expressions of opinion herein are subject to change without notice.  
Neither the delivery of this Official Statement nor any sale made under it shall, under any circumstances, 
give rise to any implication that there has been no change in the affairs of the City since the date hereof. 
Any statements made in this  Official Statement that involve matters of opinion or estimates, 
whether expressly stated to be such, are made as such and not as representations of fact or certainty, and no 
representation is made that any of those statements have been or will be realized.  This Official Statement 
contains statements relating to future results that are “forward-looking statements,” within the meaning of 
Section 27A of the Securities Act of 1933 as amended, and Section 21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 
1934, as amended.  Words such as “plan,” “estimate,” “project,” “budget,” “anticipate,” “expect,” “intend,” 
“believe” and similar terms are intended to identify forward-looking statements.  The achievement of results 
or other expectations expressed or implied by such forw ard-looking statements involves known and 
unknown risks, uncertainties and other factors that are difficult to predict, may be beyond the City’s control 
and could cause actual results, performance or achievements to be materially different from any results, 
performance or achievements expressed or implied by such forward -looking statements.  The City 
undertakes no obligation, and does not plan, to issue any updates or revisions to such forward-looking 
statements. 
Information in this Official Statement that has been derived by the City from its official records 
and other sources is believed by the City to be accurate and reliable. Information other than that obtained 
from official records of the City has not been independently confirmed or verified by the City.

BOND ISSUE SUMMARY 
The information contained in this Bond Issue Summary is qualified in its entirety by the entire 
Official Statement, which should be reviewed in its entirety by potential investors.  Defined terms have the 
same meaning herein as elsewhere in the Official Statement. 
Issuer: City of Cleveland, Ohio 
 
Issue: $29,675,000 City of Cleveland, Ohio Water Pollution Control 
Revenue Bonds, Series 2024 
 
Dated Date: Date of issuance 
 
Interest Payment Dates: May 15 and November 15 of each year, beginning May 15, 2025. 
 
Principal Payment Dates: November 15 of the years indicated on the inside front cover. 
 
Optional Redemption: The Series 2024 Bonds maturing on or after November 15, 2034 are 
subject to redemption at the option of the City prior to their stated 
maturities, on any date on or after May 15, 2034, in whole or in part 
(in whole multiples of $5,000), at a redemption price equal to 100% of 
the principal amount redeemed, plus accrued interest to the date fixed 
for redemption. 
 
Denominations: The Series 2024 Bonds shall be issued in one lot as fully registered 
bonds in denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof. 
  
Purpose: To provide funds to the City’s Department of Public Utilities, Division 
of Water Pollution Control to (a) pay costs relating to the acquisition, 
construction and improvement of the System, (b) fund the Debt Service 
Reserve Requirement for the Series 2024 Bonds, and (c) pay the costs 
of issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds. 
 
Security: The Series 2024 Bonds are special obligations payable solely from and 
secured by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the Special 
Funds, subject to bankruptcy laws and other laws affecting creditors’ 
rights and to the exercise of judicial discretion.  The Series 2024 Bonds 
do not constitute a pledge of the full faith and credit of the City. 
 
Parity Bonds: The Series 2024 Bonds are issued and secured under the Trust 
Agreement on parity with the Outstanding Bonds and any Additional 
Bonds that may be subsequently issued. 
 
Rate Covenant: As described herein under “SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF 
THE BONDS” – Rate Covenant.” 
 
Debt Service Reserve 
Requirement: 
 
An amount equal to the least of (i) 10% of the original aggregate 
principal amount of the Series 2024 Bonds, (ii) the maximum annual 
debt service on the Series 2024 Bonds, and (iii) 125% of the average 
annual debt service on the Series 2024 Bonds, which as of the date of 
issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds is $1,956,000.  
iv 
 
Additional Bonds Test: As described herein under “SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF 
THE BONDS – Additional Bonds.” 
 
Credit Ratings: “Aa3” by Moody’s Investors Service, Inc. and “AA-” by S&P Global 
Ratings.  
 
Tax Matters: In the opinion of Squire Patton Boggs (US) LLP, Bond Counsel, under 
existing law, (i) assuming continuing compliance with certain 
covenants and the accuracy of certain representations, interest on the 
Series 2024 Bonds is excluded from gross income for federal income 
tax purposes and is not an item of tax preference for purposes of the 
federal alternative minimum tax imposed on individuals and (ii) 
interest on, and any profit made on the sale, exchange or other 
disposition of, the Series 2024 Bonds are exempt from all Ohio state 
and local taxation, except the estate tax, the domestic insurance 
company tax, the dealers in intangibles tax, the tax levied on the basis 
of the total equity capital of financia l institutions, and the net worth 
base of the corporate franchise tax.  Interest on the Series 2024 Bonds 
may be subject to certain federal taxes imposed only on certain 
corporations. 
 
Legal Opinion: Squire Patton Boggs (US) LLP, Cleveland, Ohio 
 
Trustee: Zions Bank, a Division of ZB, National Association, Pittsburgh, 
Pennsylvania 
 
Municipal Advisors: Government Capital Management, L.L.C., Cleveland, Ohio and 
Phoenix Capital Partners, LLP, Philadelphia, Pennsylvania 
 
Book-Entry Only System: The S eries 2024 Bonds will be initially issued as fully registered 
bonds, issuable under a book-entry only system, initially registered in 
the name of The Depository Trust Company (“DTC”) or its nominee. 
There will be no distribution of the Series 2024 Bonds to the ultimate 
purchasers. The Series 2024 Bonds in certificated form as such will not 
be transferable or exchangeable, except for transfer to another nominee 
of DTC or as otherwise described in this Official Statement. The 
principal of and interest on the Series 2024 Bonds will be payable by 
wire transfer made to DTC. 
 
Delivery and Payment: It is expected that delivery of the Series 2024 Bonds in definitive form 
will be made through DTC on or about August  15, 2024. The Series 
2024 Bonds will be released to the Underwriters against payment in 
federal funds.

Relating to 
 
CITY OF CLEVELAND, OHIO 
WATER POLLUTION CONTROL REVENUE BONDS, 
SERIES 2024 
 
INTRODUCTION 
The City of Cleveland, Ohio (the “City”) is furnishing this Official Statement, including the cover 
page and appendices, to provide certain information in connection with the issuance and sale of its 
$29,675,000 City of Cleveland, Ohio Water Pollution Control Revenue Bonds, Series 2024 (the “Series 
2024 Bonds”).  The Series 2024 Bonds and any series of Outstanding Bonds previously issued or Additional 
Bonds hereafter issued under the Trust Agreement are referred to collectively as the “Bonds.”  All 
capitalized terms used but not otherwise defined in this Official Statement shall have the meanings ascribed 
to them in the Trust Agreement.  See “ A
PPENDIX B – DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN TERMS 
AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST AGREEMENT.”  
All financial and other information presented in this Official Statement relating to the City has been 
provided by the City from its records, except for information expressly attributed to other sources.  The 
presentation of information, including tables of receipts from sewer revenues and other sources, is intended 
to show recent historical information, and is not intended to indicate future or continuing trends in such 
revenues or the financial position or other affairs of the City.  No re presentation is made that past 
experience, as shown by that financial and other information, will necessarily continue or be repeated in 
the future.  See also “R
EGARDING THIS OFFICIAL STATEMENT.” 
This Official Statement should be considered in its entirety, and no one subject discussed should 
be considered less important than any other by reason of its location in the text.  Reference should be made 
to laws, reports or documents referred to in this Official Statement for more complete information regarding 
their contents. 
References to provisions of Ohio law, whether codified in the Ohio Revised Code (the “Revised 
Code”) or uncodified, or of the Ohio Constitution, are references to current provisions.  Those provisions 
may be amended, repealed or supplemented from time to time. See “ C
ERTAIN INVESTMENT 
CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Changes in Law.” 
This Official Statement and continuing disclosure documents of the City are intended to be made 
available through the Electronic Municipal Market Access (“EMMA”) website of the Municipal Securities 
Rulemaking Board (“MSRB”).  The City has deemed this Official Statement to be final for the purposes of 
paragraph (b)(3) of SEC Rule 15c2-12 (the “Rule”). 
Prior to issuance and delivery of the Series 2024 Bonds, copies of the Trust Agreement, General 
Bond Ordinance and the Series 2024 Bond Ordinance may be obtained at the office of the City’s 
Department of Finance, 601 Lakeside Avenue, Cleveland, Ohio 44114; thereafter, copies will be available 
for inspection at the designated corporate trust office of the Trustee.

ISSUER 
The City is a municipal corporation duly organized and validly existing under the Charter of the 
City (the “Charter”) and the Constitution and laws of the State of Ohio (the “State”).  See “ THE CITY OF 
CLEVELAND” herein. 
The Division of Water Pollution Control (the “Division”) is a division of the City’s Department of 
Public Utilities. The City owns, and the Division operates, cleans and maintains the network of sewers in 
the City (the “System”).  The System carries sanitary sewage, combined stormwater and sewage, and 
industrial waste from their points of collection to sewage processing facilities for treatment and disposal by 
the Northeast Ohio Regional Sewer District. The System also collects stormwater, which is discharged to 
the environment at various locations throughout the City.  See “T
HE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION 
CONTROL” herein. 
THE SERIES 2024 BONDS 
Authorization 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued under authority of Article XVIII of the Ohio Constitution, 
the Charter of the City, Ordinance No. 29- 16 passed by the Council of the City on January 25, 2016 (the 
“General Bond Ordinance”), Ordinance No. 898-2023 passed by the Council of the City on September 18, 
2023 (the “Series 2024 Bond Ordinance”) and a Certificate of Award delivered pursuant thereto (the 
“Certificate of Award,” and together with the General Bond Ordinance and the Series 2024 Bond 
Ordinance, the “Series 2024 Bond Legislation”).  The Series 2024 Bonds will be secured by t he Trust 
Agreement described below. 
Purpose 
The City is issuing the Series 2024 Bonds to provide funds to (i) pay Capital Costs relating to the 
acquisition, construction and improvement of the System, (ii) fund the Debt Service Reserve Requirement 
for the Series 2024 Bonds, and (iii) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds. 
The acquisition, construction and improvement projects to the System to be funded with the 
proceeds of the Series 2024 Bonds include, but are not limited to, the following: constructing and installing 
replacement sewers and repairing and rehabilitating existing sewers throughout the City as needed; 
rehabilitating and relining sewers at various locations in the City; rehabilitating and repairing sewer service 
connections throughout the City; identifying and eliminating illicit discharges; replacing or rehabilitating 
pump stations; increasing the capacity of sewer lines at various locations throughout the City to reduce the 
risk of flooding to properties, basement flooding, and st reet flooding; and acquiring equipment and 
professional services.  For additional information concerning the projects to the System, see “T
HE DIVISION 
OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL — Capital Improvement Programs” and “ APPENDIX E - FEASIBILITY 
REPORT – SECTION 6.2 – Projects to be Funded with the Series 2024 Bonds.”   
Terms 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued and secured pursuant to the Master Trust Agreement, dated 
April 14, 2016 (the “Master Trust Agreement”), by and between the City and Zions Bank, a Division of 
ZB, National Association, Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania, as trustee (the “Trustee”), as supplemented by the 
Second Supplemental Trust Agreement, dated August  15, 2024, by and between the City and the Trustee 
(the “Second Supplemental Trust Agreement” and, together with the Master Trust Agreement, as previously 
supplemented by the First Supplemental Trust Agreement, dated April 14, 2016, by and between the City  
3 
and the Trustee (the “First Supplemental Trust Agreement”), and as may be further amended and 
supplemented from time to time, the “Trust Agreement”). 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued under the Trust Agreement in the aggregate principal amounts 
set forth on the inside cover page hereof.  The Series 2024 Bonds will be dated their date of delivery, w ill 
bear interest from that date as described herein, payable semiannually on May 15 and November 15 of each 
year (each, an “Interest Payment Date”), commencing May 15, 2025 and will mature November 15 in the 
years and in the principal amounts set forth on the inside front cover page of this Official Statement.  Certain 
of the Series 2024 Bonds are subject to redemption prior to maturity.  See “T HE SERIES 2024 BONDS – 
Redemption of the Series 2024 Bonds” herein.  
The Second Supplemental Trust Agreement establishes that the Debt Service Reserve Requirement 
for the Series 2024 Bonds is an amount equal to the least of (i) 10% of the original aggregate principal 
amount of the Series 2024 Bonds, (ii) the maximum annual debt service on the Series 2024 Bonds, and (iii) 
125% of the average annual debt service on the Series 2024 Bonds, which as of the date of issuance of the 
Series 2024 Bonds is $1,956,000. 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be issued initially as fully registered bonds without coupons and in 
authorized denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof (“Authorized Denominations”). 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee of DTC, and held 
in the custody of DTC pursuant to DTC’s book-entry only system.  Purchases of beneficial interests in the 
Series 2024 Bonds will be made in book-entry form, without certificates. 
If at any time the book-entry system is discontinued for the Series 2024 Bonds, the City will take 
the actions necessary to provide for the issuance of Series 2024 Bond certificates to the Holders of the 
Series 2024 Bonds.  See “A
PPENDIX G – BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.” 
So long as the Series 2024 Bonds are held by DTC or its nominee, Cede & Co., in book-entry 
only form, the Trustee will recognize and treat DTC or its nominee, Cede & Co., as the Holder of the 
Series 2024 Bonds for all purposes under the Trust Agreement, provided that the Trustee will 
recognize Beneficial Owners for purposes of the purchase of book-entry interests.  See “APPENDIX G 
– BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.”  Each Beneficial Owner is responsible for observing the procedures 
of DTC, the Direct Participant, any Indirect Participant and the Trustee, as set forth in the Trust 
Agreement, in order to permit the timely observance of the tender process with respect to Book-Entry 
Interests. 
Payment of Principal and Interest 
The principal of and premium, if any, on the Series 2024 Bonds will be payable to the registered 
owner (initially DTC or its nominee) upon their presentation and surrender at the designated office of the 
Paying Agent.  The Series 2024 Bonds will bear interest on their unpaid principal amounts payable on each 
Interest Payment Date.  Interest on the Series 2024 Bonds will be payable by check or draft mailed or 
delivered on the Interest Payment Date to the registered holder (initially DTC or its nominee) at the address 
shown on the Register as of the close of business on the last day of the calendar month next preceding such 
Interest Payment Date; provided that, so long as the Series 2024 Bonds  remain in book-entry form, DTC 
(or any successor depository company) may direct the Trustee to make such payment by wire transfer of 
immediately available funds on each Interest Payment Date.  
4 
Transfer and Exchange of the Series 2024 Bonds; Persons Treated as Holders 
The person in whose name any Series 2024 Bond is registered will be deemed and regarded as the 
absolute owner thereof for all purposes, and payment of or on account of the principal or purchase price 
(which is an amount equal to the principal a mount thereof plus, if such purchase date is not an Interest 
Payment Date therefor accrued and unpaid interest thereon to such purchase date) of and interest on the 
Series 2024 Bonds will be made only to or upon the order of the registered owner thereof or his or her legal 
representative.  All such payments will be valid and effective to satisfy and discharge the liability upon that 
Series 2024 Bond to the extent of the sum or sums so paid. 
So long as the Series 2024 Bonds are held in book- entry form, transfers of the Series 2024 Bonds 
by Beneficial Owners may be made only as described in “A
PPENDIX G – BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.”  
At any other time, any Series 2024 Bonds may be transferred or exchanged only upon the books kept for 
the registration and transfer of Series 2024 Bonds as provided in the Trust Agreement. 
Redemption of the Series 2024 Bonds 
Optional Redemption.  The Series 2024 Bonds maturing on or after November 15, 2034 are subject 
to redemption at the option of the City prior to their stated maturities, on any date on or after May 15, 2034, 
in whole or in part (in whole multiples of $5,000), at a redemption price equal to 100% of the principal 
amount redeemed, plus accrued interest to the date fixed for redemption. 
Mandatory Sinking Fund Redemption.  The Series 2024 Bonds which are being issued as term 
bonds will be subject to mandatory sinking fund redemption prior to maturity, as set forth below: 
The Series 2024 Bonds maturing on November 15, 2049 in the amount of $6,630,000 (the “2049 
Term Bonds”) are subject to mandatory sinking fund redemption in part by lot prior to maturity at a 
redemption price equal to 100% of the principal amount thereof to be redeemed, plus interest, if any, 
accrued thereon to the date fixed for redemption, on each November  15 of the years and in the principal 
amounts set forth below: 
Year  Principal Amount

If not previously redeemed, there will remain $1,460,000 principal amount of 2049 Term Bonds to 
be retired at stated maturity on November 15, 2049.  2049 Term Bonds redeemed by optional redemption 
or purchased for cancellation may be credited against the mandatory sinking fund redemption requirements. 
The Series 2024 Bonds maturing on November 15, 2054 in the amount of $8,455,000 (the “2054 
Term Bonds”) are subject to mandatory sinking fund redemption in part by lot prior to maturity at a 
redemption price equal to 100% of the principal amount thereof to be redeemed, plus interest, if any, 
accrued thereon to the date fixed for redemption, on each November 15 of the years and in the principal 
amounts set forth below:

Selection of Bonds to be Redeemed.  If less than all of the Series 2024 Bonds that are stated to 
mature on different dates are called for redemption at one time, the maturities of the Series 2024 Bonds that 
are to be called will be determined by the City in its sole discretion.  If less than all of the Series 2024 Bonds 
of a single maturity are to be redeemed, the selection of the Series 2024 Bonds to be redeemed, or portions 
thereof in amounts of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof, so long as the Series 2024 Bonds remain in 
book-entry form, will be made by the Depository (or any successor Depository) in accordance with the 
Depository’s procedures and otherwise will be made as specified by and selected at the sole discretion  of 
the City.  In the case of a partial redemption of the Series 2024 Bonds by lot when the Series 2024 Bonds 
of Authorized Denominations greater than $5,000 are then outstanding, each $5,000 unit of principal thereof 
shall be treated as though it were a separate Series 2024 Bond of the denomination of $5,000.   
Notice of Redemption.  The Trustee shall cause notice of any redemption of Series 2024 Bonds to 
be (a) mailed to the Holders of all Series 2024 Bonds to be redeemed at the addresses appearing in the  
Register and (b) transmitted by Electronic Means to each Depository and to the MSRB, by means of its 
EMMA system.  Each such notice shall be sent not more than 45 nor fewer than 20 calendar days prior to 
the redemption date.  Selection of book- entry interests in the Series 2024 Bonds called, and notice of the 
call to the owners of those interests called, is the responsibility of the Depository pursuant to its Rules and 
Procedures and of its Participants and Indirect Participants.  Any failure of the Deposi tory to advise any 
Participant, or of any Participant or any Indirect Participant to notify the book-entry interest owners, of any 
such notice and its content or effect will not affect the validity of any proceedings for the redemption of 
any Series 2024 Bonds. 
Each notice of redemption will (a) identify the Series 2024 Bonds to be redeemed (specifying the 
CUSIP numbers, if any, assigned to the Series 2024 Bonds), (b) specify the redemption date and the 
redemption price, (c) set forth the name, address and telephone number of the person from whom 
information pertaining to the redemption may be obtained, and (d) state that on the redemption date the 
Series 2024 Bonds called for redemption will be payable at the Designated Office of the Trustee, that from 
that date interest will cease to accrue, and that no representation is made as to the accuracy or correctness 
of the CUSIP numbers printed therein or on the Series 2024 Bonds.  No defect affecting any Series 2024 
Bond, whether in the notice of redemption or the delivery thereof (including any failure to mail such notice), 
shall affect the validity of the redemption proceedings for any other Series 2024 Bonds. 
If at the time of mailing of notice of redemption of Series 2024 Bonds as described above, there 
shall not have been deposited with the Trustee moneys or Government Obligations sufficient to redeem all 
Series 2024 Bonds called for redemption, the notice of redemption will state that the redemption is 
conditional upon the deposit of moneys or Government Obligations with the Trustee not later than the 
redemption date in an amount sufficient to pay the redemption price of all Series 2024 Bonds or portions 
of Series 2024 Bonds that are to be redeemed on the applicable redemption date, and the notice will be of 
no effect and the Series 2024 Bonds will not be redeemed unless such moneys or Government Obligations 
are so deposited.  
6 
Effect of Redemption.  If moneys sufficient to pay the redemption price of Series 2024 Bonds to 
be redeemed have been deposited with the Trustee on or prior to the redemption date, then such Series 2024 
Bonds (or the portion thereof to be redeemed) will become due and payable on the redemption date, and 
interest on such Series 2024 Bonds will cease to accrue from and after the date of redemption. 
Purchase in Lieu of Redemption 
By their acceptance of the Series 2024 Bonds, the Holders irrevocably grant to the City the option 
to purchase any Series 2024 Bond that is redeemable by optional redemption on any date on which the 
Series 2024 Bond is so redeemable at a purchase price no less than the redemption price to be paid to 
Holders upon optional redemption.  The City may exercise such option by written request delivered to the 
Trustee within the time period specified in the Trust Agreement, as described above.  In the case of the 
purchase of less than all of the Series 2024 Bonds, the particular Series 2024 Bonds to be purchased will 
be selected in accordance with the provisions of the Trust Agreement as though such purchase were a 
redemption or in such other manner as the City directs. 
Revision of Book-Entry System; Replacement Bonds 
The Trust Agreement provides for issuance of fully registered Series 2024 Bonds (“Replacement 
Bonds”) directly to assignees of DTC or its nominee only in the event that the use of the book-entry system 
is discontinued for the Series 2024 Bonds.  If the discontinuance of a securities depository book-entry 
system for the Series 2024 Bonds is not the result of City action or inaction, the delivery of Replace ment 
Bonds will be at the expense (including printing costs) of any persons requesting such Replacement Bonds.  
In the event that the book-entry system is discontinued, Series 2024 Bonds will be transferable or 
exchangeable for fully registered Series 2024 Bonds of any denomination or denominations authorized by 
the Trust Agreement in the aggregate principal amount equal to the unmatured and unredeemed principal 
amount of, and bearing interest at the same rate and maturing on the same date as, the Series 20 24 Bonds 
being transferred or exchanged.  Replacement Bonds will be transferable or exchangeable at the Designated 
Office of the Registrar or any Authentication Agent, without charge (except any tax, fee, or other 
governmental charge required to be paid wi th respect to the exchange or transfer).  See “A
PPENDIX G – 
BOOK-ENTRY ONLY SYSTEM.”

SECURITY AND SOURCES OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS 
General 
The Series 2024 Bonds will be special obligations of the City and will not represent or constitute a 
general obligation, bonded indebtedness or a pledge of the general credit or taxing power of the City, the 
State of Ohio or any political subdivision thereof.  The holders of the Series 2024 Bonds will not have the 
right to have excises or taxes levied by the City, t he State of Ohio or the taxing authority of any political 
subdivision thereof for the payment of debt service charges. See “CERTAIN INVESTMENT 
CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Limited Obligations.” 
Upon issuance and delivery, the Series 2024 Bonds will be secured under the Trust Agreement on 
parity with all Outstanding Bonds previously issued and any Additional Bonds subsequently issued 
thereunder.  After the issuance of the Series 2024 Bonds, the aggregate principal amount of Outstanding 
Bonds (including the Series 2024 Bonds) issued under and secured by the Trust Agreement will be 
$57,755,000.  See “OUTSTANDING BONDS AND OTHER OBLIGATIONS – Outstanding Bonds” and “CERTAIN 
INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Additional Bonds.” 
Sources of Payment 
Under the terms of the Trust Agreement, the Bonds are special obligations payable solely from and 
secured by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the Special Funds, subject to bankruptcy laws and 
other laws affecting creditors’ rights and to the exercise of judicial discretion. See “C
ERTAIN INVESTMENT 
CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Limited Obligations” and “ CERTAIN INVESTMENT 
CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Bankruptcy.” The Net Revenues generally consist of the Revenues 
derived from the ownership or operation of the System and income derived from the investment of the 
Funds and Subfunds under the Trust Agreement, less the Operating Expenses thereof.  The Special Funds 
consist of (i) the Construction Fund, (ii) the Debt Service Fund, (iii) the Debt Service Reserve Fund (to the 
extent that a series of Bonds is secured by the Debt Service Reserve Fund), (iv) the Subordinated Debt 
Service Fund, (v) the Rate Stabilization Fund, (vi) the Contingency Fund, and (vii) the Balance Subfund.  
8 
See “APPENDIX B – DEFINITIONS AND SUMMARY OF CERTAIN TERMS AND PROVISIONS OF THE TRUST 
AGREEMENT – Pledge of and Lien on Net Revenues and Special Funds; Funds and Subfunds.”  Any pledge 
of or lien on any revenues, money or other intangible property not in the custody of the Trustee will be 
valid and enforceable only to the extent permitted by law. 
Rate Covenant 
The City covenants in the Trust Agreement, subject to all applicable requirements and restrictions 
imposed by law, that at all times it will prescribe, charge and collect such rates, rentals and other charges 
for the use of the services of the System and shall restrict the Operating Expenses of the System in such a 
way that Net Revenues Available for Debt Service (adjusted for purposes of clause (i) as described in th e 
following sentence) in each Fiscal Year shall be not less than the greater of (i) 120% of Debt Service on all 
Bonds then Outstanding payable during that Fiscal Year or (ii) 100% of the sum of: (A) Debt Service on 
all Bonds then Outstanding payable during that Fiscal Year, (B) all required deposits to the Debt Service 
Reserve Fund during that Fiscal Year,  (C) all required deposits to the Subordinated Debt Service Fund and 
to any reserve fund securing Subordinated Indebtedness during that Fiscal Year, (D) all required deposits 
to the Contingency Fund during that Fiscal Year, and (E) debt service payable on any other obligations 
payable from the Balance Subfund and deposits to any reserve funds securing such other obligations during 
that Fiscal Year.  For purposes of clause (i) of the preceding sentence, but not for the purpose of clause (ii) 
of the preceding sentence, “Net Revenues Available for Debt Service” for any Fiscal Year shall include any 
amounts transferred from the Rate Stabilization Fund to the Revenue Fund during such Fiscal Year, but 
shall be reduced by any amounts transferred from the Revenue Fund to the Rate Stabilization Fund during 
that period. For purposes of determining the City’s compliance with the rate covenant set forth herein, the 
amount of any Direct Payments received by the City or the Trustee in any Fiscal Year shall be credited 
against (i) Debt Service in such Fiscal Year if such Direct Payments related to Bonds or (ii) debt service on 
Subordinated Indebtedness in such Fiscal Year i f such Direct Payments related to Subordinated 
Indebtedness. The City currently is not receiving any Direct Payments.  
If in any Fiscal Year the Net Revenues Available for Debt Service shall be less than the amount 
required under the Trust Agreement, the City shall, within thirty (30) days following receipt by the City of 
its audited annual financial statements and the written request of the Trustee, employ a Consulting Engineer 
to make recommendations within forty -five (45) days as to a revision of the rat es, fees and charges or 
Operating Expenses or methods of operation of the System, if any, that will result in producing the amount 
so required in the next succeeding Fiscal Year.  The City covenants and agrees, promptly upon its receipt 
of such recommendations, to revise the rates, fees, and charges or Operating Expenses or methods of 
operation of the System and to take such other action as shall be in conformity with such recommendations 
to the extent the City feasibly may do so and to notify the Trustee of the actions it has taken.   
Upon the taking by the City of such actions, its failure to comply with the foregoing requirements 
shall not constitute an Event of Default. See “C
ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS 
– Changes in Market Conditions; Conditions of the City; Ability to Charge Rates.” 
Debt Service Reserve Fund 
The Trust Agreement establishes a Debt Service Reserve Fund and permits the City to establish a 
Debt Service Reserve Requirement for each Series of Bonds.  The Trust Agreement requires that if on any 
Interest Payment Date, the amount in the subaccount in the Interest Subfund or the Principal Subfund for 
any Series of Bonds shall be less than the amount required to be therein on deposit, the Trustee shall, after 
deposits are made,  if any, into the Subordinated Debt Service Fund, the Contingency Fund, the Rate 
Stabilization Fund, and the Balance Subfund, apply the amounts in the applicable Subfund, if any, in the 
Debt Service Reserve Fund to the extent necessary to make good any such deficiency (or the entire amount  
9 
in the applicable Subfund if less than sufficient).  The City may, so long as it will not result in a reduction 
of the rating assigned to any of the Bonds, substitute for funds on deposit in the Debt Service Reserve Fund 
a letter of credit, surety bond or other credit enhancement facility issued by a Qualified Financial Institution. 
The City has established a Debt Service Reserve Requirement for the Series 2024 Bonds and a 
deposit will be made to the Debt Service Reserve F und for the Series 2024 Bonds in amount equal to the 
Debt Service Reserve Requirement.  
Additional Bonds 
The City may issue Additional Bonds (i.e., additional Series of Bonds payable from Net Revenues 
and secured by the Trust Agreement on parity with the Outstanding Bonds, the Series 2024 Bonds and any 
other Series of Bonds hereafter issued) for the purposes of (a) paying Capital Costs or (b) refunding, 
including advance refunding, for any lawful purpose, any Outstanding Bonds or Subordinated Indebtedness 
where such refunding will not adversely affect the exclusion of the interest on any Tax-Exempt Bonds from 
gross income for purposes of federal income taxation.  Additional Bonds shall be equally and ratably 
payable from Net Revenues and shall be secured by a pledge of and lien on the Net Revenues and the 
Special Funds on a parity with any other then Outstanding Bonds (subject to the provisions of the Trust 
Agreement providing for the application thereof).  
For any Series of Additional Bonds that the City issues for the payment of Capital Costs or for the 
purpose of refunding Subordinated Indebtedness or other obligations other than Outstanding Bonds, the 
City must furnish the Trustee with either (A) a Certificate of the Director of Finance certifying that the Net 
Revenues Available for Debt Service for the preceding Fiscal Year or any consecutive twelve (12) calendar 
months during the eighteen (18) -month period immediately preceding the date of original issuance of the 
proposed Series of Bonds (in each case, the “Test Period”) are in an amount not less than the greater of (1) 
120% of maximum annual Debt Service on all Bonds then Outstanding and on the proposed Series of 
Additional Bonds or (2) 100% of the sum of: (a) maximum annual Debt Service on any Bonds the n 
Outstanding and on the proposed Series of Bonds, (b) all required deposits to the Debt Service Reserve 
Fund, (c) all required deposits to the Subordinated Debt Service Fund and to any reserve fund securing 
Subordinated Indebtedness, (d) all required deposits to the Contingency Fund, and (e) debt service payable 
on any other obligations payable from the Balance Subfund and deposits to any reserve funds securing such 
other obligations, during that Test Period (the amounts described in clauses (a) through (e ) being referred 
to collectively as the “Test Amount”), or (B) a Certificate of the Director of Finance, which may be, but is 
not required to be, accompanied by or based upon a Certificate of a Consulting Engineer, certifying that the 
Adjusted Net Revenues  for the Test Period are in an amount not less than the greater of (1) 120% of 
maximum annual Debt Service on any Bonds then Outstanding and on the proposed Series of Bonds or (2) 
100% of the Test Amount during that Test Period.   
No certification shall be required for any Series of Bonds being issued for the purpose of refunding 
Outstanding Bonds, provided that the issuance of the refunding Bonds will not result in any increase in 
Debt Service in any Fiscal Year; otherwise, the same certification shall be required as for a Series of Bonds 
for the payment of Capital Costs.  
For purposes of determining the City’s compliance with the Additional Bonds test, the amount of 
any Direct Payment received or expected to be received by the City or the Trustee in any Fiscal Year shall 
be credited against (i) Debt Service in such Fiscal Year if such Direct Payment relates to Bonds or (ii) debt 
service on Subordinated Indebtedness in such Fiscal Year if such Direct Payment relates to Subordinated 
Indebtedness. See “C
ERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS AND RISK FACTORS – Additional Bonds.” The 
City currently is not receiving any Direct Payment.  
10 
Subordinated Indebtedness 
The City may, at any time and from time to time, issue or incur Subordinated Indebtedness for the 
purpose of financing any Capital Costs to the System, provided that such Subordinated Indebtedness is 
secured solely by, and is payable solely from, moneys on deposit in the Subordinated Debt Service Fund, 
or the Balance Subfund, or both. Any Supplemental Trust Agr eement providing for the issuance of 
Subordinated Indebtedness shall provide that the trustee for such Subordinated Indebtedness shall have no 
right, power or authority to cause acceleration of such Subordinated Indebtedness unless and until the 
Trustee has exercised its power to accelerate the Bonds. See “ CERTAIN INVESTMENT CONSIDERATIONS 
AND RISK FACTORS – Subordinated Indebtedness.”

Shaded funds are held by the City.  Unshaded funds are held by the Trustee. 
 
(1) Debt Service Reserve Requirement: As of any date of calculation with respect to any Series of Bonds, as specified in the 
Supplemental Trust Agreement applicable thereto, but subject to the requirements of the Master Trust Agreement. 
 
(2) Contingency Fund Requirement: $1,000,000 or such higher amount  as the Director of Public Utilities may from time to 
time specify (in writing delivered to the Trustee). Subsequent to any such specification, the Director of Public Utilities may 
reduce the Contingency Fund Requirement from the specified amount, but not below $1,000,000.  The City presently has a 
balance of $1,078,000 in the Contingency Fund. 
 
Revenue Fund.  So long as any of the Bonds remain Outstanding, all Revenues of the System are 
required to be deposited in the Revenue Fund, which, pursuant to the Trust Agreement, will be held by the 
City as a trust fund separate and distinct from all other funds and moneys of the City (except for purposes 
of investment).  In each month, the amounts in the Revenue Fund shall be deposited in the Operating 
Subfund and first applied to the payment of Operating Expenses.  Thereafter, the balance in the Revenue 
Fund up to the Working Capital Reserve shall be deposited in the Working Capital Reserve Subfund and  
12 
retained as a reserve for the payment of Operating Expenses and  used for that purpose if the Operating 
Subfund shall have been fully expended. Thereafter, the balance in the Revenue Fund shall be paid at the 
times and in the amounts as follows.  
Debt Service Fund.  To the Debt Service Fund: 
(i) To each subaccount in the Interest Subfund in the Debt Service Fund, monthly and 
on or before the last day of each month (or such other date as may be provided in any Supplemental 
Trust Agreement), after giving effect to amounts therein on deposit, an amount such that, if the 
same amount were paid in each of the months preceding the next Interest Payment Date, the 
aggregate of the amounts so paid would be sufficient to pay the interest due and payable on that 
next Interest Payment Date on all Outstanding Bonds of the Series to which such subaccount 
relates; and 
(ii) To each applicable subaccount in the Principal Subfund in the Debt Service Fund, 
monthly and on or before the last day of each of the twelve months that precede a month in which 
a Serial Maturity Date occurs or a Sinking Fund Installment is due (or such other date as may be 
provided in any Supplemental Trust Agreement), after giving effect to amounts therein on deposit, 
an amount such that, if the same amount were so paid in each of the months preceding the next 
Serial Maturity Date or the next Sinking Fund Installment, the aggregate of the amounts so paid 
would be sufficient to pay the principal due on that next Serial Maturity Date or that next Sinking 
Fund Installment on all Outstanding Bonds of the Series to which such subaccount relates. 
Debt Service Reserve Fund.   To the subaccount established in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, 
monthly and on or before the last day of each month (or such other date as may be provided in any 
Supplemental Trust Agreement), commencing on the date set forth in the applicable Supplemental Bond 
Ordinance with respect to any Series of Bonds for which the Debt Service Reserve Requirement is to be 
deposited in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, after giving effect to any amounts already on deposit therein 
and pledged to such Series of Additional Bonds, an amount such that, if that same amount were deposited 
in equal monthly installments, the aggregate of the amounts so deposited in such subaccount would be equal 
to the Debt Service Reserve Requirement with respect to such Series of Additional Bonds on the fifth (5th) 
anniversary of such commencement date.  
Thereafter, if the amount on deposit in such subaccount at any time is less than the Debt Service 
Reserve Requirement with respect to such Series of Additional Bonds, the City shall pay to the Trustee for 
deposit in such subaccount, on or before the last day of each month following the date of such deficiency, 
an amount equal to one -twelfth of such deficiency.  The frequency and amount of any deposits requi red 
shall be subject to adjustment pursuant to the Trust Agreement so that the deposits required into the Debt 
Service Reserve Fund for any Series of Bonds shall be no less frequent than the deposits required into the 
Debt Service Fund for the principal of and interest on such Bonds. 
Subordinated Debt Service Fund. To any custodians of the Subordinated Debt Service Fund for 
deposit therein, such amounts as are required to be deposited therein on such dates as are specified in the 
Supplemental Trust Agreemen t or other contracts between the City and the holder or holders of the 
Subordinated Indebtedness.  If any Supplemental Trust Agreement or other contract between the City and 
the holder or holders of Subordinated Indebtedness requires the establishment and funding a reserve account 
related to such Subordinated Indebtedness, then any required deposits to such reserve account may be made  
13 
after any deposits otherwise required into the Subordinated Debt Service Fund but before any deposits 
required into the Contingency Fund and the Rate Stabilization Fund. 
Contingency Fund.  To the Contingency Fund, monthly on or before the last day of each month 
on which the balance in the Contingency Fund is less than the Contingency Fund Requirement, not less 
than one-twelfth (1/12) of the amount by which the Contingency Fund Requirement exceeds the balance. 
“Contingency Fund Requirement” means $1,000,000 or such higher amount as the Director of Public 
Utilities may from time to time specify (in writing delivered to the Trustee ) as the Contingency Fund 
Requirement. Subsequent to any such specification, the Director of Public Utilities may reduce the 
Contingency Fund Requirement from the specified amount, but not below $1,000,000. The City presently 
has a balance of $1,078,000 in the Contingency Fund. 
Rate Stabilization Fund.   To the Rate Stabilization Fund, on any date on which deposits are 
required into the Debt Service Fund, the Debt Service Reserve Fund, the Subordinated Debt Service Fund, 
and the Contingency Fund, and after all such deposits are made, any amounts that the City elects to make 
to the Rate Stabilization Fund. 
Balance Subfund. To the credit of the Balance Subfund, on the first day of each Fiscal Year or on 
the first practicable date thereafter, the City shall deposit any balance remaining in the Operating Subfund 
and the Working Capital Reserve Subfund in excess of the Working Capital Reserve at the end of the 
preceding Fiscal Year; provided that the City may at any time provide for semiannual or quarterly deposits 
of such Net Revenues to the Balance Subfund. 
Direct Payments. Upon receipt of any Direct Payment, the City or the Trustee shall cause it to be 
deposited (i) in the appropriate subaccount in the Debt Service Fund if such Direct Payment relates to 
Bonds, and (ii) in the appropriate account in the Subordinated Debt Ser vice Fund if such Direct Payment 
relates to Subordinated Indebtedness, and shall cause it to be applied solely to the purposes to which the 
Trust Agreement permits funds in such subaccount and account to be applied. The City currently is not 
receiving any Direct Payment. 
Rebate Fund. The Trust Agreement establishes the Rebate Fund as a separate deposit account 
(except when invested as therein provided) in the custody of the Trustee and requires separate accounts to 
be created in the Rebate Fund for each Series of Bonds that are Tax-Exempt Bonds. The Trust Agreement 
requires that, at least five days prior to the end of the fifth (5th) Bond Year and each fifth (5th) Bond Year 
thereafter for each Series of Bonds, including the Series 2024 Bonds, and within five (5) days after the date 
on which all outstanding Bonds of such Series are paid or deemed paid in full, the City shall calculate, or 
shall furnish information to and engage an independent certified public accounting firm to calculate, the 
Rebate Amount as of the end of that Bond Year or the date of such final payment. Within thirty (30) days 
after the end of the fifth (5th) Bond Year and every fifth (5th) Bond Year thereafter, the Trustee, acting on 
behalf of the City and at the written direction of the City, shall pay to the United States in accordance with 
Section 148(f) of the Code from the moneys then on deposit in the applicable account in the Rebate Fund 
an amount equal to 90% (or such greater percentage not in excess of 100% as the City may direct the Trustee 
in writing to pay) of the Rebate Amount determined from the date of the original delivery of the Bonds of 
that Series (less the portion of the Rebate Amount, if any, previously paid to the United States).  Within 
sixty (60) days after the payment in full of all outstanding Bonds of such Series and upon written direction 
of the City, the Trustee shall pay to the United States in accordance with Section 148(f) of the Code from 
the moneys then on deposit in the applicable account in the Rebate Fund an amount equal to 100% of the  
Rebate Amount determined from the date of the original delivery of the Bonds of that Series to the date of 
such payment (but less that portion of the Rebate Amount, if any, previously paid to the United States) and 
any moneys remaining in the applicable account in the Rebate Fund following such payment shall be paid 
to the City.  Notwithstanding anything to the contrary, the moneys needed for any payment required as set  
14 
forth herein may be derived from balances in any of the Special Funds other than the Debt Service Fund 
and the Debt Service Reserve Fund, and the City agrees to apply those balances to that purpose in the 
following order: the Balance Subfund, the Rate Stabilization Fund, the Contingency Fund, the Subordinated 
Indebtedness Fund and any related reserve fund or account, and the Construction Fund.  
If all the gross proceeds of the Bonds of any Series, within the meaning of Section 148(f) of the 
Code, are expended for the governmental purpose for which that Series of Bonds was issued within six (6) 
months of the date of issuance of that Series and it is not expected that any other gross proceeds of that 
Series of Bonds will arise in the future, then the requirements set forth herein apply only to gross proceeds 
of that Series of Bonds, if any, that actually do subsequently arise.  
Uses of Funds.  No payment needs to be made into a Fund if the moneys in such Fund are equal to 
the required Fund balance, if any.  Amounts in the various Funds discussed above are required and permitted 
to be used as follows: 
(i) The Debt Service Fund shall be used only for the payment of Debt Service Charges 
on Bonds and, to the extent provided in the Trust Agreement, for the purchase for cancellation or 
redemption of Bonds. 
(ii) The Debt Service Reserve Fund shall be used only to make up any deficiency in 
the Debt Service Fund with respect to Debt Service Charges on Bonds that are secured thereby, 
subject to the requirement that amounts in the Balance Subfund, the Rate Stabilization Fund, the 
Contingency Fund, and the Subordinated Debt Service Fund be applied to make up such deficiency 
prior to drawing from the Debt Service Reserve Fund. 
(iii) The Subordinated Debt Service Fund shall be used to make up any deficiency in 
the Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any deficiency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, to the 
extent necessary, subject to the requirement that amounts in the Balance Subfund, the Rate 
Stabilization Fund, and the Contingency Fund be applied to make up such deficiency prior to 
drawing from the Subordinated Debt Service Fund. The remaining amounts on deposit in the 
Subordinated Debt Service Fund shall be applied to the payment of the principal of and interest and 
any premium on Subordinated Indebtedness as and when due or to the required funding of any 
special reserve account established for any Subordinated Indebtedness. 
(iv) The Contingency Fund shall be used to make up any deficiency in the Subfunds in 
the Debt Service Fund or any deficiency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, to the extent necessary, 
after first drawing on the Balance Subfund and the Rate Stabilization Fund, and otherwise may be 
used by the City for the payment of Capital Costs or for the purpose of redeeming Bonds. 
(v) The Rate Stabilization Fund shall be used to make up any deficiency in the 
Subfunds in the Debt Service Fund or any deficiency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, after first 
drawing on the Balance Subfund. In addition, the City may from time to time transfer amounts on 
deposit in the Rate Stabilization Fund to the Revenue Fund and cause them to be app lied as 
Revenues.  
(vi) The Balance Subfund shall be used to make up any deficiency in the Subfunds in 
the Debt Service Fund or any deficiency in the Debt Service Reserve Fund, and may be used for 
any lawful System purpose, including, but not limited to, transfers to the Subordinated Debt Service 
Fund for payment of the principal of and interest on any Subordinated Indebtedness and the funding 
or replenishment of any special reserve account established for any Subordinated Indebtedness, but  
15 
amounts on deposit in the Balance Subfund may not be transferred or credited to the Rate 
Stabilization Fund. 
(vii) The Rebate Fund is not pledged to the pa yment of Bond Service Charges, is not 
one of or part of any of the Special Funds, and is free and clear of any lien thereunder.  At the 
written request of the City, any moneys held as pa rt of the Rebate Fund shall be invested or 
reinvested by the Trustee in Eligible Investments.

THE CITY OF CLEVELAND 
Introduction 
The City is a municipal corporation and political subdivision of the State of Ohio (the “State”).  It 
is located on the southern shore of Lake Erie and is the county seat of Cuyahoga County in northeastern 
Ohio.  The City was incorporated as a village in 1814 and became a city in 1836.  For a more extensive 
discussion of the City, see “A
PPENDIX A – INFORMATION REGARDING THE CITY.” 
City Government 
The City operates under and is governed by the Charter, which was first adopted by the voters in 
1913 and has been and may be further amended by the voters from time to time.  The City is also subject 
to certain general State laws that are applicable to all cities in the State.  In add ition, under Article XVIII, 
Section 3 of the Ohio Constitution, the City may exercise all powers of local self -government and may 
exercise police powers to the extent not in conflict with applicable general State laws.  The Charter provides 
for a mayor-council form of government. 
Legislative authority is currently vested in a 17 -member City Council (“Council”).  All Council 
members are elected from wards.  The terms of Council members and the Mayor are four years.  The current 
terms of the Mayor and Council members expire on January 5, 2026.  The Council fixes compensation of 
City officials and employees and enacts ordinances and resolutions relating to City services, tax levies, 
appropriating and borrowing money, licensing and regulating businesses and trades, and other municipal 
functions.  The presiding officer is the President of Council, who is elected by the Council members.  Blaine 
A. Griffin was elected as President of Council for the term beginning January 3, 2022.  The Clerk of Council 
is appointed by Council. 
Pursuant to Section 25- 1 of the Charter, City Council is required to redivide the City into wards 
based on the City’s population based on the 2020 U.S. Census.  As a result of this requirement, City Council 
is required to adopt a division plan that will reduce the number of wards to 15 by April 1, 2025 for the next 
regular municipal election in November 2025. 
The City’s chief executive and administrative officer is the Mayor who is elected by the voters for 
a four-year term.  The Mayor may veto any legislation passed by Council.  A veto may be overridden by a 
two-thirds vote of all members of Council.  Justin M. Bibb was elected Mayor of the City for a term 
beginning January 3, 2022. 
The Charter establishes certain administrative departments and Council may establish divisions 
thereof or additional departments.  The Mayor appoints all of the directors of the City’s departments. 
Financial Administration 
The responsibilities for the City’s major financial functions are vested in the Director of Fina nce.  
The Director of Finance is responsible for preparing and implementing the City’s current operating budget 
and capital improvement plan, collecting the City’s revenues, and procuring the City’s goods and services 
and making payments therefor.  The Director of Finance is also responsible for maintaining an effective 
system of internal accounting control that includes the maintenance of a centralized accounting system and 
the supervision of the City’s internal audit staff.  Preparation and issuance of the City’s internal and external 
financial reports are supervised by the Director of Finance.  
19 
James Hartley was sworn in as the Director of Finance for the City on an interim basis on July 18, 
2024.  Mr. Hartley was previously Assistant Finance Director since April 2007 and has also previously 
served as City Treasurer from 2008 to 2024.  Mr. Hartley was the Chief Investment Officer for the Ohio 
Treasurer of State from 1999 until 2007.  As a member of the Treasurer’s senior staff, he was responsible 
for overseeing and directing the State’s investment program, including the State Operating Fund, STAR 
Ohio Local Government Investment Pool, and the State Tobacco Settlement Funds. 
Mate Rogonjic was named Assistant Finance Director in March 2024. Prior to joining the City, he 
served in two separate roles at the Ohio Auditor of State’s Office, as the Assistant Chief Forensic Auditor 
in the Special Investigations Unit for two years and Assistant Chief Auditor in the Performance Audit 
Division for 12 years. From April 2012 to February 2022, Mr. Rogonjic was the Finance Director of the 
City of Chardon, Ohio and responsible for managing the overall finances. 
Natalie Banks is the City’s Treasurer.  She was appointed in October 2023.  Prior to that, Ms. Banks 
has served in a number of roles within the City’s Treasury Division, including ten years as Fiscal Manager 
and most recently as Deputy Treasurer from October 2013 to September 2023.   Before joining the City in 
1999, Ms. Banks was employed six years as an Operations Analyst for the Ohio Credit Union League and 
five years as an accountant for TransOhio Savings Bank. 
Lesly Camargo is the City’s Controller.  Ms. Camargo was appointed in July 2024.  Prior to her 
appointment, Ms. Camargo was the Deputy Finance Director of the City of Miami Beach, Florida.  From 
2018 to 2023, Ms. Camargo was the City’s Assistant Controller, and served as Acting Controller from 2021 
to 2022.  Ms. Camargo began working at the City in 2010 as an accountant after several years in private 
practice. 
James Gentile was appointed as the Administrative Manager for the Department of Finance in July 
2024.  Prior to his appointment to the newly- created position, Mr. Gentile had been the City’s Controller 
since 2002.  From 1995 to 2002, Mr. Gentile was Deputy Auditor for the Auditor of State’s Office where 
he planned and supervised audits of cities, school districts and other local government agencies.  From 1991 
through 1995, he was employed by the City as an accountant and, in his final year, as Acting City Controller.  
Mr. Gentile also served as Acting Director of Finance and then Director of Finance from January 1, 2021 
until February 14, 2022. 
Elizabeth C. Hruby has served as the City’s debt manager since 1996.  She is the Assistant Secretary 
to the Sinking  Fund Commission.  She has been employed by the City since 1982 when she began as a 
Budget Analyst in the Office of Budget and Management.  She was promoted to Operating Budget Manager 
in 1987 and was responsible for the development and monitoring of the City’s annual operating budget.  
From January 7, 2002, until April 1, 2002, Ms. Hruby served as interim Director of Finance for the City. 
T
HE DIVISION OF WATER POLLUTION CONTROL 
Overview and History 
The Division is responsible for managing the sanitary sewage and stormwater collection system 
and for overseeing matters relating to the elimination, control and regulation of water pollution within City 
limits. The City derives its authority to own and operate a water pollution control utility from the municipal 
utility provisions in Article XVIII, Sections 4, 5, 6 and 12 of the Ohio Constitution and Section 1 of the 
Charter. The City is empowered by such provisions to establish rates and charges for the services provided 
by the Division, acquire property, and construct facilities to provide sewage and stormwater collection 
services throughout its Service Area and perform other necessary functions to operate and maintain the 
Division.  
20 
The Division was created for the purpose of supplying sewer services to customer s within the 
Cleveland metropolitan area. Embarking with a rudimentary system in the late 1800’s, the Division 
developed as the City itself expanded. Until the early 1970’s, the City operated the entire system and 
managed all aspects of sewage treatment an d disposal.  In 1972, a court order (the “1972 Court Order”) 
created the Northeast Ohio Regional Sewer District (“NEORSD”) and transferred the operation of all 
wastewater treatment plants and interceptors to the NEORSD in December 1973. The City retained 
responsibility for the sewer collection system in the City. The Division services a significant portion of the 
entire Cleveland metropolitan area by managing the sanitary sewage and storm water drainage collection 
system. The sewer collection system transfe rs sanitary and storm sewage from its point of origin to an 
interceptor sewer or treatment plant for processing by NEORSD. The System is comprised of 11 pump 
stations, approximately 1,444 miles of sewer lines, 36,000 manholes and 43,500 catch basins and re lated 
equipment. 
Service Area 
The Service Area of the Division includes all residential, commercial, governmental, and non-profit 
customers located within City limits. The Service Area also includes customers that are physically located 
outside City limits but whose water meters are located within City limits.  
Sewer Collection 
The Division has responsibility for sewage and stormwater collection within the City. The Division 
is responsible for cleaning, maintaining, repairing and improving the System, which carries sanitary and 
storm sewage and industrial waste (which may require pre-treatment) from their points of origin to sewage 
processing facilities for treatment and disposal by NEORSD. Protecting the health and environment of City 
residents and visitors is vitally important to the Division.  
The System includes three types of sewers. The most prevalent type is sewer pipes that collect and 
transfer combined sanitary and stormwater flows. Approximately seventy-two percent (72%) of the System 
is combined sewers. The System also includes separate sanitary and storm sewers, as well as a third category 
of segmented block pipe wherein separate sanitary and storm sewers are encased within the same segmented 
block pipe.  
Stormwater Management 
In addition to operat ing and maintaining the System, the Division is the stormwater manager for 
the City. A steering committee consisting of representatives from the Division, the Cuyahoga Soil and 
Water Conservation District, and the City’s Department of Public Works, the Office of Sustainability, the 
Department of Law, the Department of Building and Housing, the Cleveland City Planning Commission, 
the Division of Waste Collection and Disposal, the Office of Capital Projects, and the City Council support 
the management of the stormwater system and compliance with the City’s Small Municipal Separate Storm 
Sewer System (“MS4”) permit.  
Non-point stormwater runoff is rainwater and snowmelt that flows over solid, impervious surfaces 
such as streets, sidewalks and parking lots. Hard, compact soil also can prevent stormwater from infiltrating 
the ground, which can lead to street flooding and erosion. Stormwater runoff can carry debris, chemicals, 
sediment or other pollutants on the ground into sewer catch basins and can flow into loca l waterways 
untreated. This can cause contamination of drinking water and compromise recreation areas along Lake 
Erie, which is Northeast Ohio’s main source of drinking water.   
21 
The Division’s responsibilities include overall management and reporting on stormwater 
compliance including compliance with the Six Minimum Control Measures specified in the MS4 permit. 
Of these six measures, the Division is responsible for the first three: Public Education and Outreach, Public 
Involvement and Participation, and Illi cit Connection Detection and Elimination. The City’s Department 
of Building and Housing is responsible for the fourth and fifth minimum control measures:  Construction 
Site Stormwater Runoff Control and Post Construction Stormwater Runoff Control. The City’s Department 
of Public Works and other affected departments are responsible for the sixth minimum control measure of 
Pollution Prevention and Good Housekeeping. 
The City complies with Environmental Protection Agency (“EPA”) requirements to maintain its 
stormwater permit. The City’s Public Involvement and Public Education (“PIPE”) program focuses on 
educating the entire community, but pays particular attention to i ts separate sewer areas, which have 
separate sewer pipes for stormwater and wastewater. In those areas, also called MS4 areas, runoff is 
discharged untreated into local waterways. Those discharges can cause water pollution and flooding.  
Public education is an important component of the Division’s authority as the City’s stormwater 
manager. Annually, the Division participates in numerous community events to inform residents and others 
about how their personal actions related to stormwater runoff can impact water quality and impede the free-
flowing capacity of the System. 
The Division promotes the use of low-impact best management practices (“BMP”) to help prevent 
flooding, protect stream channels and improve water quality. Examples of BMPs suitable for resid ential 
and commercial properties are green roofs covered with grass and plants to absorb rain water, downspouts 
connected to rain barrels to collect rain water for re- use, rain gardens with native plants that absorb large 
amounts of water, and pervious pavements that absorb and filter rain water. 
Organizational Structure 
The Department of Public Utilities has three primary, revenue- generating divisions: the Division, 
the Division of Water and Cleveland Public Power.  The Division of Fiscal Control and the O ffice of 
Utilities General Administration provide general administration, accounting, cash management and other 
financial services to the other divisions. 
The Division is administered and controlled by the Commissioner of Water Pollution Control, who 
manages all of the personnel, procurement, budget and overall operations of the Division, including the 
System. The Commissioner of Water Pollution Control reports to the Director of Public Utilities, who 
reports to the City’s Chief Operating Officer, who reports to the Mayor. The Deputy Commissioner of 
Water Pollution Control assists the Commissioner of Water Pollution Control in managing the Division.  
Key Management Personnel 
Director of Public Utilities – Martin J. Keane, as Director of the City of Cleveland Department of 
Public Utilities, is responsible for management and oversight of the Divisions of Water, Water Pollution 
Control, Cleveland Public Power, Fiscal Control, and the Office of Utilities Gen eral Administration. The 
Department of Public Utilities consists of more than 1,800 employees and a budget of approximately $661 
million. Before taking the position of Director in January 2021, Mr. Keane served as the Assistant Director 
of Public Utilities.  In this role, Mr. Keane had oversight of the entire department, with a focus on Cleveland 
Public Power, Human Resources, and Security for the Department. Prior to his role at Department of Public 
Utilities, Mr. Keane served as a City of Cleveland Councilman for over 12 years, where he was Chairman 
for the Transportation Committee and then the Utilities Committee. In addition, he was a member of 
Finance, Development Planning and Sustainability, Operations and Rules Committees. Mr. Keane earned  
22 
a law degree from the Cleveland Marshall College of Law and a Bachelor of Science from The Ohio State 
University. 
Chief Financial Officer of Public Utilities  – Catherine Troy became the Chief Financial Officer 
of the Department of Public Utilities in April 2023.  Ms. Troy started with the City of Cleveland in 2007 as 
Deputy Auditor for the Division of Internal Audit.  She transferred to the Department of Public Utilities in 
2012 as a Senior Finance Manager.  Ms. Troy has experience in costs of service and rate studies, budgeting, 
capital planning, debt, payroll, and accounts payable.  Prior to joining the City, she worked for the Ohio

University. 
Commissioner of Water Pollution Control – Ramona Lowery-Ferrell has served as Commissioner

Commissioner of Water Pollution Control in June 2023 and has been nominated to serve as interim

Service Worker. 
Chief Information Officer of Public Utilities – Mark Lasic became the Chief Information Officer

He earned a Master’s degree in Computer Engineering with a focus on Operations Research from Case 
Western Reserve University and a Bachelor’s degree in Mechanical Engineering with a focus on Physic s 
from Cleveland State University.   
Employees and Employee Relations 
The Division’s personnel budget for Fiscal Year 2024 includes 165 full-time, six apprentice sewer 
service workers and two student assistant apprentice positions. Of this amount, 126 full-time positions and 
one apprentice position were filled as of December 2023.  
Each of the full -time and apprentice employees of the Division is an employee of the City. 
Approximately 85% of the Division’s employees belong to one of nine collective bargaining units 
represented within the City. Currently 19 employees of 26 budgeted positions, primarily upper -level 
professionals and administrators, do not belong to unions. The City has contracts with eight of the nine 
unions representing 81% of the workforce, which are effective from April 1, 2022 through March 31, 2025. 
The City and remaining union are continuing to negotiate on the outstanding agreement. At this time, the 
Division does not anticipate that the current or new contracts will have any material im pact on the 
Division’s operations or financial projections.  
23 
There have been no significant labor disputes or work stoppages in the City within the last 25 years. 
Interactions with NEORSD; Key Permits 
Prior to 1973, the City was responsible for both wastewater collections and wastewater treatment. 
Beginning in December 1973, the ownership and operation of all of the wastewater treatment plants and 
interceptors were transferred to NEORSD by the 1972 Court Order. 
The Division’s discharge of flows to the NEORSD interceptor system for transfer and treatment at 
one of NEORSD’s wastewater treatment plants is governed by the City’s Community Discharge Permit for 
sanitary sewers and the City’s Community Combined Discharge Permit (collectively, the “Discharge 
Permits”) for combined stormwater and sewers. Neither Discharge Permit has an expiration date; however, 
the Discharge Permits may be modified from time to time as necessary to reflect the changing needs and 
circumstances of NEORSD and the Division. The Division is  required to submit a Compliance Report 
Checklist to NEORSD on an annual basis to demonstrate the Division’s compliance with the Discharge 
Permits and NEORSD’s BMP guidelines.  
The City consistently maintains compliance with the Discharge Permits’ requirements that require 
implementation of a number of BMPs. Under its Community Discharge Permit for sanitary sewers, which 
represents less than 13% of the collection by the System, a peak flow limitation of 14.284 million gallons 
per day is imposed at the Grayton Road connector. Under its Community Combined Discharge Permit for 
combined sewers, no peak flow limits or restrictions are currently imposed. However, NEORSD has the 
right to impose future limitations if required. No limitations, however, are anticipated to be imposed in the 
foreseeable future.  
Discharge of separated storm water for the Division is regulated by the City’s MS4 permit. A new 
MS4 permit was issued on April 1, 2021, and expires March 31, 2026. Only a small portion of the System 
consists of separated stormwater sewers. The majority of the System is combined storm and sewer service 
that is regulated under the City’s Discharge Permits.  
Customer Base 
The Division provides services to approximately 119,000 active metered water connections that 
represent essentially 100% of the population of the City, including all residential, commercial, industrial, 
governmental, and non- profit customers. The table below illustrates the average number of active water 
metered accounts in 2023 broken down by meter size (and homestead rate accounts whose charges are not 
dependent upon meter size). The largest percentage of Division customers (96%) are residential (who 
typically are served by 5/8 inch water meters), while the remaining 4% of the customers are primari ly 
commercial, governmental, and industrial accounts.

consumption per customer account is expected as customers continue to upgrade to water-efficient fixtures

Projected Customer Accounts and Consumption 
The Division is conservatively projecting continued decreases in consumption in Fiscal Years 2024 
through 2028. A 2.0% annual decrease in consumption is being projected to account for potential decreases 
in customer usage and other unknown circumstances. This projection is greater than the Division of Water’s  
25 
projections for water consumption because the Division’s decreasing consumption trend has been greater 
than the Division of Water’s. The total number of customers is projected to remain static. The number of 
customers is based on buildings with metered water service that are connected to the System. As long as a 
building is connected to the System, the customers in the building will be billed a fixed charge regardless 
of the amount of water consumed. The Division does not anticipate any net disconnection of buildings or 
establishments from the System in the foreseeable future.
